## \#204 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2018-10-26T03:02:42.632Z Reads: 66

```
I love it on the Vanguard. I chose Flex1.  4WD is spectacular.  So much more traction with the brakes. It out accelerates everything else even when the other rider is half my weight.  Top speed is 48.3 kph and it takes seconds to get there.  

I highly recommend swapping pivot bushings.  Bones Yellow barrel bushings on the bottom.  Yellow Bones Cone bushings on the top.  Watch my videos for instructions on mechanically connecting the remotes together.  I also recommend connecting the two batteries together to balance the power levels.  If you don't, then one drive will run out of power before the other.

Power down as soon as the remote vibrates or within a minute of the third blue dot flashing.  This will protect your battery from damage. Expect about 13 km of range.  Avoid riding in cold weather.  Even with 4WD, the cold weather range is limited and the voltage can drop quickly. 

The roads in my city are horrible so I turned my Vanguard into an 8 wheeled 4WD Landwheel.  Naturally you don't need to do that.  Its an interesting option if you have a band saw and a drill press.

Road vibration is minimized if you isolate the deck between a layer of rubber top and bottom.  You can do it with risers, or you can do it with 3/8 inch rubber flooring material -- the type that often goes on workshop floors.  This tip to reduce vibration works on any electric skateboard.  Landwheel L3-x already has lower vibration than most electric skate boards due to the large wheel diameter, Thick PU on the motor wheels and softer than normal PU on the motor wheels.

Make sure you have the polycarbonate shells.  If you don't, then re-inforce with a velcro strap or metal bracket.  Also, put a radius on the motor wheels before you start riding.

![image|690x217](upload://2rv46yMT0XkYtuouPQJoRhWZgBk.jpeg) 

![image|672x302](upload://e5I7rZ1xJbHLtxm5F9IXK1uF4ve.jpeg) 

![image|690x421](upload://aKZql7HeAmLcnm8lFXtfsHirYzZ.jpeg) 

![image|690x475](upload://2WjSNxsaRNIGFQZal2wEgUHarNB.jpeg) 

Videos:
[Paul's Video Play List](https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLu3dU_j2fxO4IS0gkeDMZRytqonDcmM60)


Notice that I added a teather to the rear of my skateboards.  The teather allows you to brake faster and lean forward harder prior to accelleration.  Also, if you make a mistake in your balance, the teather can be used to pull yourself back to the center of the board.  Or if you need to jump off, the teather keeps you board by your side.  Great for towing the skateboard across the street at busy intersections with high curbs.
```

Hi Germane:
If i understand the translaton correctly, you have built a double battery landwheel using the charging station as the second battery bay. YOu can now climb a 15 degree hill for 500M at 20kph and you are a 100KG rider.  This impresses you but soon after the Land wheel cuts out more safely.  The 100% brakes problem is gone. 2) The performance improvment is expected.  The voltage is droping slower so the ESC has time to power down gracefully.  This solves the 100% brakes problem.

The ESC thinks the battery is sufficient becasue of the rapid voltage recovery.  To protect the battery stop riding after the first vibration alert and most definitely after the first power down.

If I ride Gentle I can travel 14km on two battereis.  If I ride hard and fast, then only 5km.  Heavy riders always have this problem.  The advantage of the landwheel is that a heavy rider can accelerate as fast as a light rider.  But that takes a lot of energy out of the battery in a short time.  So range can be very short.

## \#213 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2018-10-27T02:32:44.587Z Reads: 70

```
Germane:

I must warn you that the V4 Brakes become much more powerful with dual batteries. The brake force is stronger when the batteries are full. Even Stronger when braking down hill. Even Stronger braking down hill with full batteries. This scale should explain:

BoostedBoard Brake strength = 10 (perfect)
V4 Landwheel Brake Strength =  20
V4 Dual Battery Landwheel Brake Strength = 25
V4 Dual Battery LW, Down Hill, Full Battery = 50  (Very dangerous, to powerful to use)

Please be careful.

Germane:

Ich muss Sie warnen, dass die V4-Bremsen mit Doppelbatterien viel leistungsf√§higer werden. Die Bremskraft ist st√§rker, wenn die Batterien voll sind. Noch st√§rker beim Abbremsen. Selbst St√§rkeres Abbremsen mit vollen Batterien. Diese Skala sollte erkl√§ren:

BoostedBoard Bremsst√§rke = 10 (perfekt)
V4 Landwheel Bremsst√§rke = 20
V4 Dual-Batterie Landwheel Bremsst√§rke = 25
V4 Dual-Batterie LW, Down Hill, volle Batterie = 50 (sehr gef√§hrlich, zu leistungsf√§hig zu verwenden)

Seien Sie bitte vorsichtig
```

## \#217 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2018-10-27T04:48:50.514Z Reads: 62

```
Yes, the black wheels look bad with wear, but its only an appearance (cosmetic).  They hold togehter very well.  They don't fall apart.  They look like they are falling apart but they actually last for a very long time.  I have never seen a broken pair.  I have 750 km on mine.

The reason for the bad appearance is that the PU is very soft for the purpose of absorbing vibration.  It works but there are many dents in the surface.

Also, you motors will not last long with the Orange PU.  It is too thin. Rocks can damage the motor.

92 mm is much safer if there are cracks in the road.  The higher center of gravity is a very small change.
```

My VESC settings are pretty standard: 50A/-50A motor, 45A/-10A battery "power mode" and 30A/-50A motor for "normal" mode :) I can do 10s and 12s with these values. ## \#225 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2018-11-30T23:22:13.033Z Reads: 71

```
Open up the compartment below the battery and disconnect the sensor wires for the motor that is locking up.  Leave connected the sensor wire for the other motor.

Let me know if it works much better afterwards.

If it works better, you can assume that the sensor wires are damaged in one of the motors.  Disconnecting the sensor wire makes the ESC run sensorless on one side.  

You want to run the other motor with sensors becasue it will help you with low speed starts.

If this fix works, you the acelleration should be almost indistinguishable from when both motors running with working sensors.

I have not had this problem myself.  However, I recall another poster having the same problem as you.
```

---
## \#226 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2018-11-30T23:30:25.748Z Reads: 71

```
Also, dont assume that the left sensor socket on the circuit board corresponds to the left motor.  They may actually cross over.  If you disconnect the three motor wirers on one  side, and then run the motors, you will know if they cross over or if left corresponds to left and right to right.

Once you figure that out, reconnect the three motor wires and diconnect the sensor corresponding to the damaged motor.
```

## \#228 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2018-12-01T09:43:14.423Z Reads: 75

```
It might have been a loose motor wire.  You may have fixed the problem by reseating the motor wire connectors.  It is also possible that a bad solder joint is present in one of the motor wires.  If that is the case, the problem might return but it could be very easy to fix with some solder.

Another possibility is a broken wire in the sensor wires.  Breaks inside the insullation can connect and disconnect depending on the position of the wire.  Moving the wires around like you did can temporarily restore the continuity.

If the problem returns, and you want to try disconnecting the sensor wires, this is not difficult to do.  The yellow glue that you have circled is not hard to remove with strong plyers or wire cutters.  Just use the plyers or wire cutters to crush and tear at the glue.  Once you break the glue's seal in a small area, the entire blob of glue becomes easy to peel off with pliers.  I find wire cutters are best for crushing the glue. You can glue them back together with hot glue if you find the sensor wire is not the problem.

One other thing to look for is this.  The landwheels with the ABS shells all  suffer from broken screw posts eventually.  when this happens the metal backing plate and the ABS shell won't be held tightly together.  That can allow wires like the sensor wires to slip between the ABS shell and the backing plate.  It is one way that the wires can be damaged.

If you have replaced your ABS shell with a PVC shell, make sure you did not pinch any wires between the shell and the backing plate during re-assembly.  Pinched wires can either break or short circuit.  Both types of problems can be intermittent. So it may be worth it for you to disassemble the backing plate to inspect the condition of the screw posts.  Prior to disassembling the backing plate you need to remove the electronics cover.  During the disassembly check that the motor wires and sensor wires are not pinched between the backing plate and the ABS shell or between the backing plate and the battery terminal block.

The fact that just assembly and re-assembly has resolved the problem suggests that there is a possibility of intermittent connecetivity of a wire or intermittent shorting of wires. 

The best case for you is that reseating the motor wire bullet connectors has fixed this permanently.  However, I think this is less likely than the various intermittent scenarios that I described above.

It's worth taking the time to track down an intermittent problem.  For example, if you are traveling along at full speed and one motor wire diconnects, then having only two motor wires connected can lock the motor into a fixed position.
```

---
## \#229 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2018-12-01T09:45:28.650Z Reads: 72

```
The way to test the motor wire bullet connectors is to gently pull each bullet connector away from the wire.  If its a bad solder connection, the connector should pull right off the wire.
```

## \#233 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2018-12-08T05:02:03.421Z Reads: 73

```
9.5 miles on a landwheel battery is far to long.  5 - 6 miles is the practical upper limit (if you power down at the appropriat battery indicator).  As soon as you hit the third flashing blue light, its time to stop immediately.  It is possible to ride longer but it puts the battery in peril.

The landwheel battery has a rapid discharge rate which gives it the wild acceleration and hill climbing.

It also has a rapid recovery rate. 

So if you ride down to the third flashing blue light, then coast or push or just ride with a very light thumb on the throttle, the battery will recover voltage. Unfortunately, the voltage recovery is a very shallow charge. 

So if you keep repeating this riding style to squeeze the maximum distance out of a landwheel battery then you are likely to destroy the battery in a single trip.

You can‚Äôt ride a landwheel battery on the last flashing blue light. As soon as the last blue light starts flashing it‚Äôs time to power down.  Easing off on the accelerator, heading down hill or anything else you do after the third light starts flashing blue is just serving to progressively ratchet the battery down below its minimum safe charge.

I did exactly the same thing myself  a year ago -- the first time I took my first L3-x for a long range ride. I ruined the battery on that one trip.  It‚Äôs just not the way the product is supposed to be ridden.  I recall the manual does say to stop riding when the third light starts flashing.

Once a LW battery is damaged, it becomes very unsafe.  The voltage tends to drop extremely fast down to nothing.  That sudden loss of all power can trigger the wheels to lock up.  I‚Äôm not sure if it‚Äôs an intentional emergency brake or if the circuit board just fails to cycle the power between the three motor wires.  I‚Äôm pretty sure it‚Äôs the second scenario, I think below a certain voltage, the ESC gets stuck in one of the three charge positions, effectively locking one or both motors in to place.

With an undamaged battery, the ESC has time to power down gracefully.  But with a damaged battery the voltage drop is so sudden that there is no time for a graceful power down.  

For the same reasons described above, you never want to power up a landwheel that has just powerd down due to low voltage.  In the time that it takes to step off the board and turn it upside down, the landwheel battery can recover enough voltage to trick the ESC into thinking it has enough power to continue.
```

---
## \#234 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2018-12-08T05:29:00.324Z Reads: 67

```
[quote="JoseMartinez, post:231, topic:45697"]
I decided to separate the wires and use heat shrink over the bullet connectors
[/quote]

If the heat shrink on the motor wires appears to have fixed your intermittent motor lock,  then the original problem was likely a bad solder joint.  I really doubt that you had a charge jumping the huge air gap between bullet connectors.  That's very implausible.

So I supect the heat shrink is only masking a bad solder joint.  I recommend you  cut off the heat shrink and tug on the bullet connectors until you find the bad connection. If you can't find the flaw then just resolder them all.

An intermittent connection on a motor wire can cause the wheels to lock in one postion.    Safety first.  An electic skateboard is not something you want to hold together wiht bubble gum, duct tape, or heat shrink.
```

I am wondering if there is already an anti spark built in the esc

If your Landwheel ESC is functioning properly, you don't need an anti spark switch.  The V2's and V3's sparked when you inserted the battery.  The V4 does not spark.

## \#247 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-03-05T09:44:08.154Z Reads: 67

```
@Byronel

Visnu has a point.  There are lots of ways to fix a landwheel.  My take on the landwheel experiment is that it all came down to the batteries.  it was an unconventional choice.  The plus side of that choice was a rapid discharge rate that supported spectacular acceleration.  The downside of the choice was that the same battery also had a rapid voltage recovery rate that allowed riders to run the battery down to automated power down, then restart the landwheel and keep running.  That was contrary to the usage instructions but alot of riders including myself did just that.  I figured that out after wrecking my first two batteries doing long range tests.  I bought 6 more batteries and none of them failed with the proper usage. So the batteries could be durable, just not in the way that many riders use them.  This problem is not unique to Skateboards.  I wrecked an EGO 54 volt chainsaw battery by over depleting it in the same way that I did to the first two land wheel batteries. Now I have a half dozen Ego power tools and batteries and no additional batteries have failed becasue I use them properly.  I've seen others wreck boosted board batteries over depleting them.  It's a characteristic of many lithium batteries that running past the first power down is the kiss of death for a battery.  Landwheel batteries did have limited range so they encouraged users to mis-use them every time the rider tried to streatch out the range.

I sympathize with your experience.  Its no fun to spend a lot of money on something and end up with it being unusable.  I also sympathize with Jason who set out to make what he though was going to be the greatest electric skateboard and encountered so many more problems than he expected.  He paid a heafty price for what in my opinion all came down to a battery that was not well suited to the expected range and usage patterns of most riders.

I overcame those limitations for my self by doubling up the drives and buying enough batteries to swap my way up to 20 kilometers of range. By rigerously powering down at the last flashing blue dot, I've traveled many hundreds of kilometers with zero battery failures.

I know Jason is trying to regroup and I wish him well.  If he learned all the lessons that were to be learned from Landwheels V1 through V5, then he may ultimately suceed.

At this point, being bitter won't get your landwheel up and running.  Vishnu has one solution which is to repurpose your landwheel hubs.  They are spectacular and can be unioned with a pair of Vescs and a conventional Skateboard battery or even a Mepo replacement battery.

However, there is a simpler solution which is to replace the battery only.  It's a pretty simple task to patch a conventional skateboard battery in to any version of the Landwheel.  The result is longer range than landwheel riders are accustomed to and virtually the same acceleration curve.

Recently, I've experimented with connecting the Landwheels up to power tool batteries.  I've actually assembled two of these.  One is made with a V2.  The second is an L3-x.  you might wonder why I did this if I have six working landwheel bateries.  The answer is that I made these as air travel boards. Landwheel battereis are questionable by some airlines becasue any lithium battery that is associated with a skateboard is questionable.  Power tool batteries are accepted without question.

Both landwheel boards work when powered by power tool batteries.  Especially the V2 (which was famously unusable when it was shipped) transforms into a top notch electric skateboard.  Power batteries are super cheap.  Two in series output 41 volts.  So far my only caution is that the V2 has no brakes when the batteries are fresh off the charger.  But moments after burning off a few joules, the V2 Brakes are rock solid.

So you have lots of options to get back on the road.  There are some private forums up here where Landwheel riders collaborate around VESC settings.  I can invite you to those forums if it interests you.

When I'm done my vacation testing of my "Rigid Landwheels"  I'll post some how to pictures, Instructions and maybe a video.
```

## \#260 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-03-13T02:00:49.435Z Reads: 62

```
[quote="Xmir, post:258, topic:45697"]
I bought a meepo battery. How hard is it to replace the original battery
[/quote]


Easy. especially if you buy the Meepo enclosure. Then you bolt the Meepo battery and enclosure to the front of the board and the L3-x drive to the back.  Two wires to jumper the meepo battery into the L3-x drive.  Suggest you disconnect the L3-x terminal block to prevent shorts and don't make any use of any damaged L3-x batteries and don't try to combine the Meepo and Landwheel battery to run them in parallel.

I'll be posting a video in a week or so showing how I replaced Landwheel batteries with power tool batteries for the purpose of a travel e-skateboard.  It worked.  But a Meepo battery would be more suitable for daily use and group rides. Get as large a battery as possible.  The L3-x is capable of massive acceleration.  But it needs a serious battery to get the most out of it. If the battery can't keep up, it will limit things like up hill acceleration.  The L3-x ESC likes a battery with 42.5 volts fresh off the charger.  Check around to see if a 36 volt Meepo battery will give you that or if there are other batteries that are more suitable. The two 18 volt power tool batteries (wired in series)  output 40.1 volts fresh off the charger.  Its barely enough.  The L3-x thinks its dealing with an almost depleted battery so its touch and go for the start-up.  Sometimes takes 20 pushes of the power to trick the ESC into starting up. I found that the power tool batteries changed with more charge cycles.  The range capacity increased dramatically but the peak charge voltage dropped marginally.  That small drop eventually made it impossible for the L3-X ESC to successfully power-up.  No such problems with the Landwheel V2 ESC.  It was built for much lower voltage.  A Landwheel V2 is actually a formidable skateboard when powered by a larger battery than came with the V2.

Since you are seeking to restore an L3-x to full function, see if you can find a Meepo rider to tell you what the peak voltage is fresh off the charger before you go out and buy one. It has to be somewhere between 41.5 and 42.5 volts for you to expect good results.  The other option is to pick just about any battery and swap out your ESC for two Vescs.  

Be careful running the L3-x on any fully charged battery with brakes.  The L3-x battery comes off the charger under charged to support full battery braking.  If the battery has no capacity to absorb the Regen current, you can fry the L3-x Esc.  So if you swap batteries to something other than Landwheel, you need to run a few blocks without brakes before braking.  MUCH LONGER BEFORE YOU  HEAD DOWN HILL.
```

---

## \#265 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-03-25T20:02:03.497Z Reads: 48

```
From your description, your charger is behaving in a manner indicaitng the Landwheel battery is damaged.  My opinion is that this is usualy as a result of over depletion.  Typically this is from trying to squeeze too much range out of the battery or continuing to ride after a power down.  For those who still have functioning landwheel battereis, its avoidable by powering down as soon as the last blue dot starts flashing. The very first vibration alert is another good signal to power down and swap.

I'm guessing Byron, that you only have one battery and that its damaged. A different BMS is not going to help you.

So connecting a different battery from another manufacturer is one good way to resurect the Landwheel.  You just need to make sure the peak voltage off the charger is up around 42 volts.  42.5 is perfect.  40 is too low.   The landwheel ESC will check the voltage when you power it up.  If it finds less than 40.5 volts, it will shut down during the start-up cycle.  So the blue light will come on for a microsecond and then turn off. I found that with 40.1 volts I could get the L3-X to start-up if I pushed the button six to 10 times.  But Below 40.1 volts it was hopeless.

A VESC is a programmable ESC designed by benjam Vedder.  It has programmable settings including minimum and maximum battery voltage.
```

## \#268 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-03-26T14:08:01.310Z Reads: 49

```
So that's interesting.  You put landwheel hub motors on the front and belt drive motors on the back.  Which power tool bateries did you use?  What are the specifications for  volts, amp hours, watt hours?  What does the volt meter say fresh off the charger with the two bateries in series?  YOu may have noticed from my video that I did something similar with 18 volt rigid batteries.  The peak voltage started off at 40.1 volts which was just barely enough to start up the L3-x.  Eventually the peak voltage was lower (after a number of charge cycles) and the L3-x would not power up any more.  I'm curious what your battereis add up to.  What's your range?  Why did you choose a hub/belt drive combination?

![image|601x326](upload://9wwaLULPqLLpGzwGyvq8F5PdSVf.jpeg)

## \#269 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-03-26T14:15:52.297Z Reads: 46

```
[quote="Byronel, post:266, topic:45697"]
I will try the six to 10 times button technique.
[/quote]

Requiring 10 button pushes to start up was an observation, not a solution.  Two power tool batteries in series output 40.1 volts which was barely enough to start-up an L3-x.  After a number of charge cycles, the peak charge voltage dropped just marginally and the L3-x would blink and then shut down during the powe-up cycle.  Extrapolating from that experiment, you need to choose a replacement battery that has the right voltage range or you need to switch to a vesc.  

Also, don't run the L3-x on damaged batteries.  They have no capacity to absorb the Regen current so you can blow the ESC during braking.
```

## \#279 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-03-27T15:04:25.623Z Reads: 45

```
Battery 1 has the correct peak voltage.  If it is in good condition otherwise, the range can vary between 2 km and 4.5 km.  Each time you ride beyond the range limit, cells can be damaged.  Temperature, weight and how hard you accellerate or ride up hill all reduce the range on each trip. The first vibration alert indicates time to power down.  If you stop at the first vibration alert and go through a charge cycle, you can gradually build up the range of most lithium batteries including the Landwheel batteries.  


Batteies 2,3,4 likely  do not have enough peak voltage to power up the landwheel. If they do, thye won't go very far.  Maybey only a few feet. Most likely one cell is damaged in each battery. Thats my guess.  Some have restored batteries like these by disassembling them and equalizing the batteries with a single cell charger.  From what I understand one cell is usually damaged beyond restoration. I have no experience with either method that  myself.  Working with lithium battery cells can be dangerous.

If you live near california, you might want to team up with @ShutterShock   He is looking for dead landwheel batteries and he has the skill to swap good cells for bad cells.  He may be able to caniblaize one of your three bad batteries to repair his own battery and maybey two of yours.

Others have gutted the Landwheel batteries and replaced the cells with tesla style cells.  But the example that I saw left no room inside the battery for a BMS so they taped the BMS to the exterior of the battery.

Other than working with @ShutterShock, your best option likely involves connecting the Landwheel to a third party battery.  Just make sure the peak voltage off the charger is in the right range.  42.5 is perfect.  41 volts might be enough as long as the peak volts don't drop too much over time.
```

## \#285 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-03-27T16:42:24.857Z Reads: 41

```
[quote="Byronel, post:282, topic:45697"]
as soon as I let go it goes green
[/quote]

It means the BMS has detected a bad cell and for safety reasons will not accept a charge from the charging brick.  Green does not mean the battery is good.  It means the charging cycle is over because the BMS is not drawing power from the brick.
```

---
## \#286 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-03-27T16:45:13.983Z Reads: 47

```
[quote="Byronel, post:283, topic:45697"]
4400mAh? Could these be used instead of the 3200mAh
[/quote]

I believe that the 25 volt V2 batteries wer 3200 MAH.  The very first V3 & V4 36 volt batteries that came out were mis labeled as 3200MAH becasue the battery sticker from the old product was used.  In fact all  of the 36 volt batteries were 4200MAH.
```

## \#290 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-03-28T21:44:31.740Z Reads: 53

```
So, that's a thing that can happen to any hub drive electric skateboard.  

I see Mike had the same thing to say and beat me by 1 minute.

I've too  have seen people post about the same type of failure happening to raptors and carvons.  I've only seen one other complaint about a landwheel motor sheering off from the trucks.  There may be more than I know of. But the one I saw previoulsy was a V3 and it looked really beat-up.

For what it's worth, I've always been terrified of loosing a wheel at speed so i've engineered my set-up so that I never need to worry about it.  8 wheels!!!

This adds som weight but it also adds tremendous safety.  The double trucks float cleanly over large cracks in the pavement.  With single trucks, getting caught in those cracks puts eormous stress on the axles and also present the risk of throwing the rider off the front if the wheels get completely locked in to a crack.  I use to hate the whalopping sound of a set of wheels dipping deep into a crack in the road.  Its a frightening sound.  Roads in Ottawa Canada are just horrible.  So this set-up fixed it all for me.

![image|690x403](upload://vU7uvgJ4CHPPmHoPch1n7cW3uJ1.jpeg) 

![image|690x382](upload://thlnEyk5g8fHzVsW0e1Eps2b7zG.jpeg) 

And like Mike said, check who wants spare parts before you toss your landwheel.  Mabey someone wants an ESC, remote, your other hub motore, etc.  I know @Vishnu was looking for motors.

Back to the topic of repacing the Landwheel battery with a different battery...I happened across an informative video form Mboards:

https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pouyqky2pF8

Mboards sells battereis:

https://www.mboards.co/collections/batteries

This is the biggest one:
https://www.mboards.co/collections/batteries/products/12s4p-complete-battery-solution

but its 44 nominal volts which could be a 52 volts or higher of peak voltage.  So that's probably too much for a landwheel ESC.

Here is the 36 volt version:

https://www.mboards.co/collections/batteries/products/10s4p-complete-battery-solution

It might be worth using the seller's contact link to find out what the peak charge voltage is.  42.5 is ideal.  40 volts is too low.

Thier batteries include a BMS inside the battery enclosure plus a charging brick.

## \#308 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-04-01T01:02:45.265Z Reads: 54

```
[quote="Kingdom421, post:272, topic:45697"]
I ran the battery in series inside the mounts. I took the mount from the drill itself
[/quote]

So I checked out my the L3-x that I had set-up as a travel board.  I thought it stopped working as a result of lower voltage from the drill batteries after several charge cycles.  It turns out my ESC won't start up even wiht a fresh L3-x battery.  My conclusion is that I likely damaged the ESC by using the drill battteries.  The most likely cause would be that the regenerative braking current had no where to go either becasue the batteries were full or because a circuit breaker internal to the drill batteries cut off the current to protect the batteries.  

The V2 Landwheel does not have the same problem yet.  I'm not sure if a VESC might have similar problems with full or overload protected batteries. 

Anyway, my conclusion from the drill battery experiment is that the most likely outcome is not a durable electric skateboard.
```

## \#318 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-04-01T14:43:47.431Z Reads: 50

```
[quote="Kingdom421, post:310, topic:45697, full:true"]
What do you mean lower voltage. Two 18v is 36v which is what a revel landwheel runs on already and actually the Milwaukees show 20v so in series you should get almost 40v
[/quote]

Yes, the two Rigid batteries in series output 41.1 volts.  But the L3-x was hard to start-up on the rigid batteries and was easy to start-up on the L3-x battery.  So when the L3-x eventually completely failed to start-up  in the dominican republic resort, I assumed the peak voltage was dropping.  That was a guess becasue I did not have a volt meter with me.  Now that I'm back home, the L3-x will not start up at all on the original L3-x battery.   The same battery easily starts up a different L3-x drive. Also, the volt meter still shows 41.1 volts from the pair of fully charged Rigid batteries.

So I believe The ESC is damaged.  It could be something else.  There might be a problem with the power button or power button cable.  It could also be a delayed reaction to the polarity reversal that occured when I built the battery from 9 volt batteries.  

![image|537x400](upload://8Nn5X3E55pNPDpbqWaDX1YEEcNG.jpeg) 

The L3-x battery has the red and black wired reversed where they connect to the battery terminals.  So I did have the 9 volt travel battery connected wiht reverse polarity for a minute.  I rode for about 40 - 50 kilometers in the dominican republic before the L3-x would not start-up any more.

I suppose the longer yours works on power tool batteries, the less likely it is that the batteries dammaged my L3-x ESC.

Full battery braking has been known to damage the L3-x ESC.  It happens when riders use V4 batteries.  V4 batteries come off the charger fully charged.  L3-x batteries come off the charger under charged.

Keep me posted on how long your L3-x  continues to work on power tool batteries.  I'm curious.  Next week, I'll try swapping parts around to see if its the entire ESC that is damaged or maybey just the power button or cable.
```

## \#350 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-04-29T09:09:33.002Z Reads: 55

```
[quote="Mikenopolis, post:348, topic:45697"]
why
[/quote]
Naturally, I recognize that 6 wheel drive looks a bit extreme at first glance.
However, I had lots of good reasons for doing this.  

I'm a big guy.  I enjoy an extra-long board that gives me a wide stance.  The roads in Ottawa are really horrible.  Every street has dozens of potentially catastrophic wheel grabbing cracks and pot holes.  Last year I found that the double trucks on each end made it possible for the board to safely float over those dangerous obstacles.  The double truck also cut road vibration down to almost nothing.  That numb feeling that a lot of riders feel after riding over dimpled pavement was eliminated.  Last year, this was a four wheel drive board.  In that form, there were so many improvements in the areas of traction, high speed steering, uphill performance, improved range, braking and acceleration.

One shortcoming last year was still range.   I had a hard time matching the range of other riders in my riding group even if I traveled with extra batteries. The landwheel batteries take a long time to recharge so I could not pick up much of a charge during 20 minute pit stops where other riders could pick up a full charge. My wife‚Äôs E-bike has a 70 km range.  So riding with her, my range was also a limitation. 
Over the winter, I experimented with different batteries.  Those experiments gave me longer range but I it made the L3-X ESC relatively slow.  The top speed and acceleration were both cut in half.  One of my ESC's also stopped functioning as a result of the experiments.

The 4 wheel drive configuration that I had last year lacked balancing wires for the batteries so the batteries were always discharging unevenly.  That was reducing my range and putting my batteries at risk of over depletion.

So this year I decided to put 4 batteries on the board with balancing wires.  I felt it was preferable to carry the extra batteries on the board instead of on my back.  Now, with four batteries in parallel, I‚Äôm expecting 20 to 30 kilometers of range without having to swap batteries.  I won‚Äôt need to fill a pack sack with spare batteries or chargers and a power bar.

Originally, I was going to assemble eight wheel drive.  However, I decided to stop at 6 wheel drive for three reasons:

1) The effort to lengthen all of the wires and run them through the board took days for the first top-mounted landwheel enclosure. It took 22 solder joints total.
2) I wanted a big headlight on the front.  That required a voltage splitter and voltage regulator.  Omitting the ESC on the front of the board was the best way to make room for those electronics.
3) The drive wheels don't steer as sharp as the conventional trucks.  So I was worried about losing too much steering radius if both front trucks were motorized.

The results are pretty cool.  I've lost 30 pounds since last year, so I'm down to 205 pounds.  But I'm still a heavy rider. I know you are a heavy rider also Mike, so I think you should be aware that guy‚Äôs like us have a hard time stopping fast in an emergency and we can also loose traction in those situations.  


With 6 wheel drive, the acceleration, braking, traction and high speed steering are just so far beyond what is possible from any 2WD board out there.  Having had the unpleasant experience of being thrown from a boosted board with a loss of rear wheel traction, I really appreciate the traction advantages of what I have now.  The reduced vibration is something that really benefits my joints because my knees and ankles are not in great shape.

I really enjoy electric long boarding, but I‚Äôm over 55 years old now.  This set-up has made the board much safer for my road conditions, weight, etc.

The lighting is also a huge advantage.  I can see 50 feet ahead of me and the entire width of the road.
```

---

## \#352 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-05-06T23:16:54.910Z Reads: 50

```
Well, I bought six  V2 Landwheels.  Jason replaced two of them wiht V4's and then sent me six L3 -x replacements.  So I have a bit of inventory to play with.

I have two boosted boards and two one wheels.  I ride them all.  But my favortie long distance board is the multi drive landwheel.  It is by far the fastest electric longboard in Ottawa.  People who have ridden lacrox boards in Montreal, tell me that the lacroix would not keep pace with my Landwheel.  thats when it was a 4WD.

My Landwheel V2 with Rigid batteries was also pretty impressive as a light weight travel board.  Huge range, strong acceleration, light weight.  The board was too short to establish top speed but it was probably 50 kph.

I've raced against Raptors  and mellow boards also.  They  were both slower -- though the mellow board surprised me to the extent it kept up.  There was a much lighter rider on the Mellow board -- but even still it was impresssive that he kept it a close race.

## \#358 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-05-07T12:55:04.530Z Reads: 55

```
FYI, 6 wheel drive seems to be a bad idea.  The new (Fresh out of the box) drive that I added to the rear stopped working within a week. Lots of possible reasons why.  I extended  all of the wires in order to top mount the ESC and battery.  The new wire lengths were not identical.  Its also possible that the rear most drive slips and sticks becasue it has less traction than the two drives in the center.  So I've decided to go back to 4WD but keep the 4 batteries.  The brakes were better modulated with 4WD than with 6WD. So an interesting experiment but 4WD wins.
```

---

## \#360 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-05-08T00:59:45.182Z Reads: 55

```
So i figured out why my third drive stopped working.  One of the 22 soldering joints that I made to lengthen the wires broke,

![image|640x475](upload://8VMaySTTUGnl2ZMVj7cwgDMk8WT.jpeg) 

So that translates into aproximately 60% brakes.  So I guess the cool thing about three drives is that if one of them goes into lock up mode, the other two drives have the combined power to keep traveling at 50 kph.

It will be interesting to see if I have damaged the ESC or if it will be all fine after I fix the solder joint.
```

## \#373 Posted by: revel_flo Posted at: 2019-05-30T17:08:16.646Z Reads: 55

```
Landwheel friends,

We have some exciting news to share. After more than a year of product development, we are super excited to launch the next version of the product.

Meet the Revel Kit! 

![DSC00672|690x459](upload://t9WZyr3V6QZw7gvQU1JUKbyi3ij.jpeg) 

We kept what was awesome about the Landwheel V5 - the ability to mount it on most decks - and expanded the versatility of the product to now include a variety of standard longboard wheels.

![compat|680x357](upload://k2DvC5yjsayKbBAi3hcCOdDKd8w.jpeg) 

The enclosure has been completely redesigned and attaches to the baseplate, securely, with copper nuts inside each mounting screw hole. The battery has been redesigned as well, now using a slide-in system instead of the click-in system from the old version. Moved away from LIPO to high-quality LI-ION Samsung cells.

I have been riding the final prototype for the past month or so and overall, I can tell you this Kit has more torque, better brakes, higher top speed and better range. 

This is my favorite setup currently: Never Summer El Jefe + ABEC 11 Flywheels 97mm

![DSC00659|500x500](upload://eoURIcSYTg8BDGmIPuTE0KYLayG.jpeg) 

We are close to mass production but need to raise additional money so we can proceed with manufacturing without needing to sacrifice anything. 

**We will be launching a Kickstarter campaign on June 4th** (tentative date!) and it would mean the world to us to have your support once again.

You will be getting first dibs at the Early Bird price of $499!

I know many of you already ride awesome boards and perhaps don't want to deal with angry wives or girlfriends about our esk8 hoarding habits :rofl:, but please consider sharing this news with friends who might be interested in joining you on the endless ride :+1:

Best,
Flo
```

## \#383 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-06-05T16:19:34.990Z Reads: 53

```
[quote="BearBoi, post:381, topic:45697"]
My Landwheel often buzzes at me going up hill on anything but eco mode.
[/quote]

I think the particular Landwheel that I ride allows me to field your question.  The Landwheel's LIPO batteries have a rapid discharge rate that allows them to accelerate up hill like its flat ground.  However, that dischsrge characteristic also allows the voltage to drop rapidly.  Landwheel batteries are also a tad low on total capacity (115 WH). When accelerating up hill with just one Landwheel battery, its not too long before the ESC detects the low voltage and the remote buzzes.

Most of you know that I build a double battery 4WD landwheel.  Even on 50% battery indicator, it can climb a 25% slope for more than a minute on full throttle.  I'm not making that up.  Its parlaiment hill in Ottawa.

More recently, I've added two extra landwheel batteries to my 4WD for a total of 4 batteries. If I ride between 20 and 30 kph the range is about 20 kilometers on 4 fully charged batteries.  But if I travel at the 49 kph that its capable of, my range drops to less than 8 kilometers.  Neither of those are great ranges considering I've quadrupled the battery capacity.

This is all to say that the low battery warnings you are getting are not as a result of heat or faulty ESC.  It all has to do with a battery choice that gave the landwheel relativley short range, particularly under hard acceleration.  Landwheel batteries can have particularly bad capacity if the rider over depletes the battery by riding on the red dot.  Red means stop.

I gave Jason suggestions based on my own battery observations.  I know many other riders echoed those recommendations.  The concensus was that the landwheel deserved a large capacity Lithium Cell battery instead of the smaller LIPO batteries.  

We  see that these suggestions were acted on with the Revel KIT.  The smallest battery is 159WH.  The Largest is 216WH.  The manufacturer is Samsung.  These are widely used battery packs that are yielding 15 - 20 mile range for other brands.

I have not had any riding  experience on the new Revel Kit.  But on paper, the battery choice addresses one of the main weaknesses of the landwheel. 

I'm really looking forward to the Revel Kit becasue I'd love to have everything that I have with my current set-up without having to lug around four to eight batteries.  I'm also looking forward to the option to mount massive 100mm plus wheels.

So I jumped in with both feet today and pledged for a double KIT with two 216 WH batteries.

![image|690x109](upload://kpryyfaiAeYdb81PVq0Ps6FouvH.png)

Good Luck Jason.  Good Luck Flo.
```

```
I posted the below on a different forum but might be good context for anyone curious to learn more:

> Unfortunately, the Kickstarter campaign did not quite kickstart! :grin: And there are a few reasons why:
> 
>1. We (ironically!) focused too much on building a solid product and did not put enough time in making sure the campaign is a success
>2. We‚Äôre also seeing a fairly negative feeling (understandable!) towards esk8 crowdfunding in Facebook groups and other mediums, mainly due to previous failed projects.
> 3. We‚Äôve got a lot of ‚Äòtoo good to be true‚Äô type comments (Ha!) Short term, this meant people who did not know us (Landwheel or Revel) thought it might be a sham. Long term, this is actually great news, as it means we managed to pack enough value to make this product a success once it‚Äôs out there!
> 
> Overall good learning experience and we definitely wish we had tackled this product launch a little bit different. Lesson learned!
> 
> Thank you to all the backers and those of you who were planning to back the project. The Revel Kit will be coming to market and the timeline might actually be shorter than it would‚Äôve been through Kickstarter.
> 
> Our website will be ready for pre-order by early next week, and for a limited time, we will be honoring the $499 discounted price from our Kickstarter!

Check out the axle shaft square part, its a weak spot in the construction and tends to break off. In the end it might lead to something @BearBoi experienced so as long as this part is still connected you sould try to fix it to the axle (real weld, JB weld epoxy glue)

## \#417 Posted by: BearBoi Posted at: 2019-06-15T11:45:24.918Z Reads: 48

```
Today I had yet another breakdown with my landwheel :( last time my motor mount broke loose and ate up my cables, also in the process it fried my hall sensor and made pretty sparks fly and threw me off the board (thankfully no injury just a sore knee) not fun though. Got that sorted, got a replacement truck from @visnu777 and a new good motor from Revel, aswell as a tool for the lug nut inside the motor. I have been riding now for a week with mostly no issues, I have had a blast, until now...

This time it's an electrical failure. Yesterday going home from work the motors were "jerking" and did not keep continous power. then it did turn itself off and lost connection completely including breaks. I then assumed it was because a connector got loose because after going down a curb I noticed the case popped loose a bit. I tightened the screws, made sure all connectors were well (I had tools with me) I rode all the way home with no more issues. The screw holes on the back plate are stripped though :/ 3  of the screws don't screw in at all.

Fast forward to today, I took it out for a quick ride to the grocery store on smooth asphalt. I got about 200 meters before it lost connection again like yesterday. This time I knew the case was intact and no cables were pulled. This time the power button does nothing, not even a flash of blue light.
Kicked it back home and opened it up.

I unscrewed everything so I can see if any cables were visibly damaged or pinched, no capacitors blown, everything looked fine. I tightened the connectors a bit more and plugged in a battery to see if there was any sign of life... Saw continuous large sparks from the battery terminals before even pressing the power button, so I quickly pulled out the battery. After further examination I notice little burn marks on almost all the the battery terminal prongs.

![IMG_20190615_121258|120x180](upload://nuUb6tCpVzzPuoRo4MmEznbz52.jpeg) ![IMG_20190615_121307|120x180](upload://cWldRx0vHvCKjWSC4s3GS6MQToO.jpeg) 

At this point I think my Landwheel is done. I don't have the tools or knowledge to further analyze and figure out what works or does not. Could be the battery terminal, or the esc, or the wires, or all of the above, and I don't know how to start debugging. What I have posted on esk8 are only the major problems, the times I haven't been able to fix it myself. I also have various cracks in my frame, stripped  and cracked screw holes I have patched up my landwheel with glue more than once. This (thing) had plastic that broke which I replaced with a strong adhesive pad underneath. My antenna cable kept getting stuck in little cracks and I worried it would get damaged and I was told it is sensitive. So I glued it to the metal frame.

![IMG_20190615_121416|120x180](upload://adIwrusKlXmxuioPB80xbxJiuY3.jpeg) ![IMG_20190615_121900|120x180](upload://uQUTwrUl8U7yEA1Ixm9w4Yk8hB6.jpeg) 

I have a cracked hall sensor, which does not work, I've been fine without it though as one working hall sensor is enough as long as I'm on flat ground.

I live on top of a large, long hill, fairly steep at times too. All the way from the inner city to my apartment is about 5 miles of mostly going uphill. That is tough for any electrical skateboard, especially for a landwheel built for rapid acceleration. I've always made it work though using eco mode or just being gentle on the throttle, I'm a light rider so it works. My batteries are all getting worse and worse though and after getting my board assembled again after a month of sitting, only one of the batteries manages to get me home and past all hills without turning off. One of the batteries shut off just from being idle. The other two work great for city use and going down hills, can't get me home though. I have 4 batteries. Only one I would say works really good, two of them decent, one seems unusable after being unused for a month (I did make sure to charge it inbetween, but still made a difference)


 ![IMG_20190615_130609%20(1)|250x180](upload://6JPV5RT606n3ACi3CjhE8sjH7Dt.jpeg)  

Despite all this I check my emails daily hoping for an update on the revel kit. Why? it promises to fix most if not all the problems I have had with my landwheel. Larger capacity batteries should mean they last me longer and are more reliable. The carbon frame means I shouldn't have to worry about cracked plastic. Going away from hub motors means not all stress is directly transfered from the wheels to the motors and to the trucks, it's more spread out. I have hope that Revel and Jason will provide a great product with great customer care which is why I'm looking forward to spending $799 for a new kit.

The Landwheel has been my main form of transportation for a couple of months now. I have put maybe  around 700 miles on the board myself. I am not the first owner hoewer, I got it for around $500 used. At that point it had no signs of breaking, all the cracks and broken components are from me, so I have no one else to blame.

Still figuring out what to do with the landwheel parts and how to move forward, I might buy another board while waiting for the revel kit, or parts to make one, or find a way to repair the Landwheel, or just bite down and wait patiently for the Revel kit and be without an esk8 for the next couple of months.

@revel_flo & Jason please make revel kit badass and reliable, and thanks for your great support and communication with the community.
```

## \#419 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-06-16T21:12:41.355Z Reads: 43

```
@BearBoi

I invited to a forum that might interest you.

Here is a second related forum:

https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/t/landwheel-hall-sensor-wiring-for-vesc/51323/4

Based on your descriptions, I'd say your ESC is fried.  This may have happened for one of four different reasons:

Damanged motors can fry an ESC
Bad batereis lack the capacity to absorb  regen current  so the ESC can be damaged braking or down hill.
Long downhill streaches on a full battery or damaged battery can do the same thing.
Brief loss of connection wiht the battery also gives the Regen current no where to go.

So if you have good motors, then a VESC conversion is your best option.  The links I gave  you have all the info you need.  Just don't use your landwheel batteries.  The discharge rate may be to high for a VESC.

If the Vesc conversion does not interest you then think about a used boosted board.  The V1's are pretty cheap.  Just check the serial number with BB to make sure its not stolen.
```

---

## \#423 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-06-20T01:53:56.640Z Reads: 42

```
So Yes.  A landwheel battery that won't take a full charge should not be used becasue it does not have enough capacity to absorb regen current.  Wiht no where to go the regen current is likely to fry the ESC.

I woudl not throw them out just yet.  One landwheel owner has created a 3D printing file for printing a deeper landwheel battery enclosure.  I think as his project moves forward, we'll see some designs for  soldering together banks of lithium ion cells and a BMS.  If you ever want to follow those instructions, you are going to need the terminal block form the old landwheel battery.

Talk to @Byronel if you want to be invited to his deeper 3D battery case thread
```

---

## \#436 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-07-07T06:41:51.144Z Reads: 40

```
So I leared a few new things about the Revel Kit.  The front Trucks are new and about a half inch wider than the L3-x Front trucks.  I did not notice that at first.  So I was using an L3-x front truck becasue I assumed ther was no difference.  With the L3-x trucks, I had a speed wobble even after tightening the pivot bushings and also upgrading to bones bushings.  After swapping the Revel Kit front Truck on to the board, the speed woble is gone.  I'm pretty sure I hit top speed with the proper trucks.  It seemed faster than 50 kph but I did not have my cell phone with me to measure top speed.  Tommorrow, I'll go for a long  ride to evaluate range.

## \#437 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-07-07T18:40:39.465Z Reads: 44

```
51.1 kph (or faster)

So I went for a long ride with my ottawa riding group. I have the 216 WH battery.

I was able to travel 17.5 kilometers on a single charge.  However, I was riding pretty fast (above 30 kph for most of the ride and the route was mostly up hill. I gained 50 feet in elevation. The last three kilometers i was riding on a solid red dot with flickers of blue.  I switched to economy mode and streached out the ride to get the next charging station.  So 17.5 KPH was an absolute maximum for my weight (206 Lbs) and the route that we took.  If I rode any further, I would have been on flashing red.  I wish I would have had a spare battery to swap in.

I then recarged over lunch.  Charging was very convenient becasue the Revel Kit has a charging port built in.  only had to carry the charging brick with me. The charge time is a little long but it seemed on par with the other boards.  ONe rider wiht a boosted board mini extended range was able to get his batery up to 92%.  I think we charged for over an hour. My charger did not switch from red to green but I was able to get up to a full charge indicator on the remote.  So I was probably also at 92%.   If I had the newer version of the remote I would have had acces to battery statistics. 

We got back on the bike paths and rode for another 15 minutes.  I dropped down one blue dot which confirmed my charge was less than 100%. 

At that point,I had a drag race with the whole riding group including a modified Evolve GT.  The GT rider had upgraded from the stock 100 KV motors to 200 KV motors.  This evolve GT was a lot faster than other evolves that I raced.

Anyway, we raced from a rolling start at 11kph.  He pulled ahead of me by about 10 feet.  That lasted for about 45 seconds-- then I blew past him.  He was probably 200  meters behind me by the time I hit top speed.

I hit 51.1 kph but had to ease off the throttle  as a matter of safety.  I would have to make some additional changes to my pivot bushings in order to have felt comfortable going faster.  I estimate the board would do at least  55 kph if I invested more time in tuning the board for high speed stability. Considering I just slapped the drive on a Loaded Talib Flex1 Dance board and swapped/tightened the pivot bushings, the stability at 51.1 KPH was pretty amazing.  

Now, the Evolve GT rider said he had to stay below 75% throttle in order to maintain control.  I believe him.  His board was very powerful.  I rode it briefly.  Punching the throttle was enough to throw many riders off the back of the board.  His brakes were good.  The Revel Kit brakes were far superior.

I think the big difference was control.  The revel Kit is a really solid ride which is why I was able to blow past him while he held back on the throttle.

Interestingly, his remote control told him that he hit 53 kph. "Map my ride" told me that I maxed out at 51.1 kph.  I'm not sure what is more accurate.  But if he actually hit 53kph, then I hit 60.  But I don't think thats the case.  51.1 kph seemed about right.

So its official, a single Revel Kit Drive is faster than a 4WD Landwheel L3x both in acceleration and top speed.

The following chart shows our drag race.  Check out the last big spike.  You can see we matched speeds at 11 kph then raced.  the acceleration curve on the Revel Kit looks like a perfect straight line on a 95 degree angle.  You can see the same behaviour in the braking curve.  I think I used almost 100% brakes to scrub off enough speed to make the right angle turn that was ahead of me.

![image|331x461](upload://fi9BZzSEZmxXHnvHmpI2m0U9WJg.png)

One last comment is that 4WD likely has some high speed stability advantages over 2WD.  I cant really make a 1:1 comparison becasue  my 4WD setup has a Loaded vanguard Deck.  But I did take the 4WD machine down the exact same path last year at 49.1 KPH and I recall it was effortless to maintain high speed control.  It took some concentration and corrections to keep the 2WD Revel kit on a tight line.  I don't know how much of that was due to the different deck choice but I'm sure some of the difference was attributable to 4WD.
```

## \#439 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-07-08T03:42:44.199Z Reads: 40

```
Same wheel diameter as the L3-x.  90 mm.

What I learned today is that maximum speed in practive depends largely on the straight line stability of the entire system.  If I had a death wish, I could have kept accelerating at least up to 55, posibly up to 60 kph. Who knows...I'm just guessing. But I had to ease back the throttle at the limits of where a minor course correction started to have twitchy outcomes.  

The same can be said of the modified Evolve GT.  The GT rider claimed he never got past 75% throttle because he was not confident the his board could maintain a steady course.  In theory, his skateboard could have out accelerated mine from start to finish.  Instead, I overtook him within 45 seconds and left him  hundreds of meters behind by the time I hit my own limit.

Considering how little time I spent setting up the board for speed I think 51.1 is pretty impressive.  Acceleration and braking were phenomenally effective.  

I should say that no one should take any electric skateboard out of the box and aim for top speed.  And that's certainly not what I did.  The night before I did ten short test runs while I swapped in better quality bushings and experimented with the tightness of the pivot bolts.  I ran out of bones Barrel  bushings so I was only able to swap out the top bushings for bones medium cone bushings. Swapping out the lower barrel bushings would have really helped the high speed stability.

It would have been extremely dangerous to attempt such a high speed with all four of the stock pivot bushings and without adjusting the pivot bolt tightness. 

Road conditions are also critical. This was also done on a perfect streatch of pavement with no cracks or potholes.
```

## \#441 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-07-08T04:04:44.961Z Reads: 36

```
Hi Jason:

It was a one time test becasue we were all curious to know how fast it could go. But I did take precautions. I have the prototype strapped together with two velcro straps becasue I know the protype is more fragile than the injection molded version will be.  I also wore full safety gear including a padded motorcycle Jacket (sholder pads, spine protector& Elbow pads), and knee & Shin pads and of course a helmet.

But if it makes you feel better, I'm finished with the high speed test and long range test.  I won't be riding it much more except for taking video and drone footage.

Congratulations on an amazing product.  The braking and acceleration are perfect.  The geometry of the trucks give a very stable ride.  The battery range is excellent.  The direct drive hub motors are very powerful with great cooling.  The 90mm complete Urethane wheels keep the vibration low and the traction is excellent.  One Revel kit accelerates faster and brakes more effectively than a 4WD landwheel.  The Revel Kit with the extended range 216 WH battery has two or three times the range compared to a 4WD landwheel with two batteries.
```

## \#444 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-07-08T15:37:14.382Z Reads: 36

```
Hi Germane:

I would love to watch a video of you racing.  It sounds like you have "mad Skills"

I think you completely understand that the most important part of speed is CONTROL.  The L3X 4WD had acceleration and braking curves that were superior to any other board I have seen.  There might be some boards that are more powerful but the power can't be controlled in a way that is usable.

The 4WD L3-x was so easy to control that other boards have no chance of keeping up.

One weakness that the L3-x had was the PU on the motor wheels.  They were slippery and the vibration was high.  

With the Revel Kit, the standard 100% Urathane wheels are a huge improvement  to vibration, traction and control.  The wider trucks also make a big difference. The truck Geometry also seems much better. 

The only weakness of the revel kit is the pivot bushings which are easy to replace and should definitely be replaced by the owner.

For those of us who love our 4WD landwheels, its hard to imagine a system that is superior in every way.  Yet the 2WD Revel Kit seems to do that. 

You are correct, by moving the drive system foward 3 inches from the standard bolt holes...

![image|638x476](upload://opL1H8CVw9aJt7Snji7nhhTVvLk.jpeg) 

...I can lift the nose for sharp turns and 180's.  It will be a hard choice for me between 4WD kit and  2WD Kit.

https://youtu.be/9oLAx4I3x3Y

## \#451 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-07-11T14:40:58.417Z Reads: 37

```
The first thing to do would be to check your battery voltage.  Assuming you have an L3-x, It should be up around 40 - 41 volts.  39 is marginal.  Below that the battery is damaged. If you can find another  36 volt battery (typically 40 volts Peak off charger) then you can test if you landwheel starts up with it.  But don't run the wheels fast and brake becasuse you can pop the ESC if the battery has no room for regen current.  Two 18 volt tool batteries connected in series  will allow you to perform the same test but the same warning applies.

What version of the landwheel do you have?
```

## \#453 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-07-15T03:53:24.283Z Reads: 39

```
I went for a long group ride today. 

![image|690x283](upload://vJz4L2K0hksX9Rm5IB1w9LPk6iE.jpeg) 

I rode the 4WD landwheel 26 km, then swapped boards and rode the  2WD revel Kit for another 13 before calling it a day.  Both the 4WD Landwheel and the Revel Kit are the fastest boards in Ottawa by far.  Its not just the acceleration and speed, its the handeling and the ability to travel fast safely and with total confidence. 

The Evolve GT and GTR are pretty fast at accelerating but they are much less stable at high speed.  The Revel Kit accelerates faster and has a much higher top speed. Its only the Modified GTR's that can beat the Revel kit for the first 10 seconds.  Then the Revel kit blows past them. The Evolve boards are too short and the double hung trucks are prone to wobble.  

There is a Mellow board rider in our groups who is half my weight.  He can keep up to me up to his top speed of 46 kph.  His drive has been replaced five times under the 2 year Mellow board warranty.  So you have to wonder how long it will last outside of warranty.  The Evolves also seem to be broken more than half the time.  Thier riders love them but they seem to ride thier back-up boards more often than their Evolves. 

One of the riders in my group has an Inboard M1.  It seemed as fast or faster than the Evolve GTR.  But neither can keep pace with the Landwheel 4wD or the Revel Kit.  None of the other boards are even close -- including the boosted boards, Own Boards, Meepo's. Exway's etc. etc.

The 2WD Revel Kit accelerates faster than the 4WD landwheel and has a higher top speed.  I'm going to try to chart both the acceleration curves for comparison.

So far the Revel Kit prototype has really been a perfect skateboard.  It out performs the 4WD L3-x on acceleration, top speed and more. One 216 WH revel Kit battery gives me the same range as 4 mint Landwheel batteries. My Revel Kit board is one third the weight of my 4WD landwheel -- and I get to tick tack around the turns becasue the nose is so light.  

The Revel Kit Trucks are wider and have much more stable geometry compared to the Landwheel.  The Standard Urethane wheels grip the road far better than the soft Landwheel motor sleeve urethane. My only caution is that the stock bushings need to be replaced immediately in order to take advantage of the Revel Kit at higher speeds. The stock bushings are only safe up to about 30 - 35 kph.  As soon as you swap in some top notch 95a Cone and barrel bushings, the Revel Kit handles like a race car  at all speeds.

The revel kit acceleration and braking curves are superior to the L3-x.  The thrust is greater but its delivered more smoothly. Acceleration is phenomenally faster than a 2WD L3-x and noticibly faster than a 4WD L3-x.  Same observation for braking.  Shorter stopping distances and perfectly smooth braking from the Revel Kit.  For those of you who found the 2WD Landwheel a little soft in the braking department, the Revel Kit fixes that.  Revel Kit braking also outperforms the 4WD landwheel.  The Revel Kit stops faster and smoother  --  very surprising becasue the 4WD has an extra set of braking wheels. I think a big part of the improvement is that the Revel Kit has much better Urethane.  But the Revel Kit braking power curve is the other big piece of the improvement

I look forward to the final product so I can buy an inventory of batteries.  With just one battery for the protoype I have to be careful about managing my range.  I can go 17 km if I ride the same speed as most riders.  But if I ride at the speeds that the revel kit is capable of the range does drop a bit (just like it does on any electric skateboard).  The extent to which range is reduced by hard acceleration and high speed  is not nearly as sever as it was for the L3-x. Nother nice thing wiht the Revel Kit is that recharge time is much shorter than it was wiht the L3-x batteries. For example, I can match both the range and recharge time of a boosted board G2+ Extended range.  I can do that even when I'm accelerating faster and traveling much faster than a boosted board is capable of.

So I'm routing for Jason and Flo to get the right number of pre-orders in place to go to production.  If you are still  sitting on the fence about whether to upgrade/pre-order, then ask me questions about the prototype.  

What I see so far is in my opinion the ultimate electric skateboard drive.  It outperforms $2500 boards and does not lock you in to any particular style or length of deck.

We L3-x owners all had a thousand suggestions for how to improve the L3-x.  Riding this prototype, I see that its all there.  Range, speed, acceleration, durability, lighter weight, less vibration, better traction, wider truck stance, better carving, improved braking more durable urethane.  It even has a USB port for lighting or for demonstrating to TSA that its a power bank.

I've got two boosted boards and I've test ridden over a dozen different boards in my riding group -- including Pleanty of  set-ups that cost over $2500.  My L3-x 4WD was always better on most dimensions but fell short on range, traction, truck geometry weight and recharge time.  The Revel is superior on every dimension except maximum range.  17 Kilometers on a single battery is good but its not "better than everyone else".  But with multiple batteries the Revel it will win on that dimension also. 

I'll try to get my review video posted.  My daughter is doing the editing.

If you have any question feel free to ask.
```

Looks really cool.  Do you have an order link for the battery holders? I assume they are not AA sized.

Also, potential risk is that if you hit a bump that causes one of the cells to disconnet for a second, you could pop the ESC.  So you might want to think about having a second battery in parallel.  Maybe a Mepo battery or something like Germane's hover board battery.

## \#468 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-09-16T18:00:31.866Z Reads: 44

```
Lemon:

The boosted board G2+ on Speed 4 definitely accellerates faster for the first few seconds.  That's because the Kit is moderating the rider's input so there are no sudden jolts.  Its safer but you won't win a short 25 to 50 meter race against a boosted board.  But as soon as the first two seconds are over, the Kit has a much stronger acceleration curve.  It catches up to and passes the boosted board.  That's my experience.

Make sure you are on the fastest Kit Speed.  I have never handled the new remote so I don't know how simple or complicated it is to change speeds.  

I think you also know that there are three different brake settings.

I found the Kit prototype brakes to be perfect for my weight.  Just like the acceleration curve, the braking curve is intended to be soft when you first  pull back on the remote.  

Make sure you are not using the remote like a boosted board remote.  On the boosted board you have to pull back on the remote a little slowly so you don't fly off the front.  With the Kit, you pull back 100% on the brakes then you can release later if you don't want to slow down as fast.

I did not test the revel Kit prototype on many hills.  Yes, a boosted board can maintain position and even back up when you are on a hill.  The Landwheel was never perfect at maintaining position on a hill.  So I understand your criticism.  

In general, the Revel Kit brakes were perfect for me.  I found them very safe and very effective.
But different riders like different things when it comes to brakes.  

Very powerful brakes are great when you use them perfectly. But when you make a mistake, they can throw you on the pavement.  So I prefer very safe brakes over very powerful brakes.

As far as top speed, treat your batteries well and they should become stronger after 6 to 12 charge cycles.  That might help you hit higher speeds.  My prototype had already been ridden by Jason for many months.  So when I recieved it,  the battery was already broken in.
```

## \#470 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-09-16T19:23:07.699Z Reads: 42

```
Stronger batteries support faster speeds because there is less voltage sag with higher capacity battereis
```

---
## \#471 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-09-16T22:29:48.778Z Reads: 42

```
[quote="murdomeek, post:469, topic:45697"]
What? You get a higher top speed after 6-12 charges? How?
[/quote]

The ESC used in the Kit is very similar to the L3-x.  Jason developed the L3-x ESC it to solve a sudden cut-out problem that occurred with the very early V4 Landwheels.  The V4‚Äôs would accelerate like a rocket until they suddenly cut out.  As an electric skateboard accelerates, the battery voltage drops. The V4 basically accelerated until it hit critical voltage and then it would cut-out.

So for the L3-x ESC, Jason programed in a pacing algorithm.  The ESC monitors the battery voltage and as the voltage drops during acceleration, the ESC throttles down to reduce load and keep the battery above critical voltage.

Consequently, a stronger battery will give you better acceleration and higher top speed.

One example of that is the L3-X riders who connected two batteries in parallel.  Their L3-X drives accelerated much faster and reached higher top speeds.

Naturally, a damaged battery has the reverse effect.

We also noticed with the L3-x that range increased from the time it was new.  Jason advised us that this would happen and I certainly observed that it was true.

My son and I notice similar improvements with our boosted boards each spring. They sits idle all winter so the first few rides in the spring have very short range. The range improves with charge cycles and gets back up to the normal range after six to ten charge cycles.

So if you put the two ideas together ‚Ä¶
  - more speed from stronger batteries
  - New batteries gain capacity with proper charge cycles

Then, it is certainly possible that the Kit top speed might improve with some proper charge cycles.

However if the batteries are over depleted then the reverse would happen.  So eskate riders should always stop on the first vibration alert instead of just slowing down to squeeze more distance out of a battery.  Think of your battery like it is a horse that you care about.  As soon as the horse is exhausted, you need to let the horse rest and you need to feed it.  If you just keep riding the horse at a slower speed, you can travel further but you are doing damage to the health of the horse.
```

---

## \#474 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-09-17T15:13:31.890Z Reads: 44

```
If you want more speed, then  A second battery in parallell or 4WD is a sure fire way to do that.  That's been my experience.  I've always used multiple L3-x batteries but others have paralled in third party batteries.

Rememer that Jason's ESC monitors battery voltage and throttles back when the voltage starts to drop.  So more amps of battery power results in less voltage sag which allows the ESC to operate without holding back

For 4WD, i'd be really surprised if the Revel Kit did not go significanlty faster than a 4WD L3-x.  I guess i'll find out soon
```

## \#475 Posted by: BearBoi Posted at: 2019-09-30T18:37:11.442Z Reads: 43

```
My revel kit arrived today. I have the range+ batteries with a 2wd kit.

I only spent about 10 minutes on the board, cruising at fairly low speed. The reason is because it's dark out and was raining earlier so pavement is slippery. Anyway, I want to get my first impressions out there.

The torque is superior to the Landwheel. I was getting wheelspins up steep hills and went 20 km/h and had to ease off on throttle (wet pavement, but still) those same hills the Landwheel struggled on and went almost walking pace.

The breaks almost got me to a complete stop down the same hill... Not quite, but almost. The Landwheel rolls significantly faster. Breaks will probably work better on dry pavement though. Will try again tomorrow.

The remote is great, beyond expectations for me. It paired instantly and automatically out of the box. The display shows all the information you need. Feels even better in the hand than the Landwheel remote, which I liked a lot. Scratches easily though, and no satisfying plastic film to peel :frowning: also wish the strap was adjustable because I have tiny wrists. It is swappable though so that is a minor complaint.

Handling is hard to judge as I haven't gone far or fast, also was on wet pavement. The bushings seem a bit too soft for my liking though. The wheels and trucks absorb vibrations well, I don't feel the need to change wheels or rubber paddings, my thoughts on that could change after more riding though.

The overall fit and finish feels premium, materials look and feel nice. Swapping batteries feels a bit stiff and hard, I will probably get used to it soon though. The charging dock is great. It is tiny and light and just snaps on. The box art is minimalistic but does the job.

It was well worth the wait, and I am a satisfied customer :)
```

## \#489 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-03T04:07:12.654Z Reads: 39

```
ok,

There are two possibilities.

the less likely possibility is that the battery is jammed on the track.  I think that's really unlikely because there is just nothing to catch on.

The more likely situation is that the button mechanism inside the battery is not properly depressing the latch that springs up from below the drive.  

The battery button is supose to push the latch down flush with the top of the drive so that the battery can slide out past the latch.

So stop trying to force it.  I'm going to make a video to try to illustrate how to release the mechanism without damaging either the drive or the battery.  

Until then, just charge the unit that you have without trying to take the battery out.  Let Jason  and Flo know you have a problem and that I'm trying to help you.

Lets keep the conversation here in this thread until we get things figured out.

@Landwheel_Jason
@revel_flo
```
