## \#496 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-03T22:51:45.865Z Reads: 36

```
@revel_flo

**Edit:
I watched the VIdeo again and its crystal clear that the bottom of the battery button is sliding off the top of the latch mechanisim tha spring up from the ESC enclosure.  The only way for this to happen is that the latch is on a 45 degree angle tilting forward.  There is no way to force the battery out of the drive.  We need to push the top of the latch towards back into a vertical position.  Then the battery button can propely engage the top of the latch.  The best way to do this is proceedure 2.  Use a slim putty knife to slide between the battery and the drive. Then use the putty knife to push the latch back to vertical.  If we get the latch back to vertical then the battery release button may work.
**End of Edit.

Flo:

I suggest that BearBois does not get two people involved in trying to forcefully release the battery.  The most likley outcome of that will be a broken shell on the drive. Specifically, the front of the shell near the latch will break off. Then you have to replace the whole drive and you never find out what the original problem was.

I think the best solution is to find a gentle way to release the mechanism.  I'm pretty sure there is no way for the track to jam the battery into place so it must be the latch that is not releasing.  If you look at the video, the button is exhibiting a stick and slip behavior.  I think the bottom of the button is slipping off of the top of the latch and the latch is not getting depressed.  I've disassembled and studied these two mechnisms.  For the stick and slip behaviour to happen, the latch is most likely leaning forward instead of perpendicular. Leaning backward is another possibility.

Potential causes:
1) improper assembly
2) Latch leaning forward --Customer pulled forward on the battery without pushing battery release or with the battery button not fuctioning properly
3) Leaning backward -- Battery hit an obstacle while in motion.

If you want to find out exactly what went wrong then you  invest in sending out a new unit and having BearBois Ship the malfunctioning Unit back to One of us (Jason, Paul or Flo).  I am confident I coudl get the battery released without further damage and I would be able to determine what happened.  Jason could probably do the same.  Your an engineer so you could probably do it also. Germane in Germany or Technotron in the Netherlands is another option.  I think they have the skills to release the battery and perform some diagnostics.

If you want to try to first try to fix this remotely then here are a few methods:

1) Procedure 1: Gently tap the battery back towards the rear of the drive. This manuver would hopefully push a latch that was angled forward in to a more vertical position.  Then hopefully the battery release mechanism would function without slippin off of the top of the latch.

2) Proceedure 2: use a very thin putty knife blade.  slide it between the drive and the battery.  See if it is possible to push the latch from a forward leaning position to a vertical position. When the latch might be vertical, depress the battery button.  Hopefully it will not slip off the top of the latch and the battery can be released.


I have a theory to offer about what might have caused the Latch to shift from vertical to angled.  When I first got my revel kit, I could not remove the battery. I hammered on it and eventually got it out.  In the process I cracked the front of the drive cover,   I later realized that I was pushing the USB cover thinknig it was the battery release button. I think that there should be some product design change like a red button to distinguish the release button from the USB port cover. I think something similar might have happened with Bearbois but I'm not saying its his fault.  The USB cover looks exactly like the release button but it is more visible than the release button.

If this is indeed what happened then repairing the unit would likely involve replacing the ESC cover plate, and the latch.  

It is also possible for the latch to be just shifted out of position. If this was the case then no replacement parts would  be needed.  The solution would be some disassembly and reassembly to get the latch back into its proper position.  I don't think the battery button would need to be replaced.  I don't think it is part of the problem.

3)Proceedurre 3: if it is not possible to remove the battery using one of the first two procedures, then this is the least destructive procedure. Use  a three inch exacto knife blade and a light hammer to cut the latch from left to right.  So, insert the exacto knife blade to the left of the latch.  Then lightly hammer the blade towards the right until the latch severs. you would need a firm hand on the knife handle while hammering. This should release the battery allowing further inspection.  I think this method is too dangerous for the customer becasue the customer could cut themselves.
```

## \#501 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-04T05:27:41.554Z Reads: 32

```
@BearBoi
CC @revel_flo  , @Landwheel_Jason 

Bear:
I have created a video to show you what I think is jammed and how to release the battery.

Before you try the procedure in the video, give the battery a little shove towards the back of the drive.  Just a quick shove with the palm of your hand.

https://youtu.be/gFsXTZWnoSE

Don't read too much in to the broken plastic.  All the plastic was 3D printed and it arrived in ottawa with alot of cracks already.  I did a real number on it the first time I tried to get the battery out. THen I rode it hard and might have hit a few obstacles.  These white 3D printed parts are not representative of the strength of the black injection molded polycarbonate plastic that makes up the Production Kit.

But I do think there is one Flaw in the Kit Design.  The rubber USB cover looks more like a battery release button than the actual button does.  I suspect @BearBoi and I both made the same mistake.  So something should be done so that others don't make the same mistake.  Posting some information is a good start.  But I think the Latch button needs to have a different color and Maybey the product should ship with two stickers.  "USB Cover"  and "Battery Release"
```

## \#504 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-04T19:25:42.979Z Reads: 31

```
@BearBoi

when you do find something thin enough, only push the latch back about 3/16th of an inch (less than 1/8th of an inch). That should be enough to get it into alignment with the bottom of the release button.

If you need something really thin, an old flat razor blade would do the job. Hot glue it to the end of a screw driver and use the non sharpened edges to push against the latch.

![image|97x60](upload://hxspVwzVqgGHWv0WIN2JT7PERuO)

![image|245x61](upload://mPucVCpr9ZBT11uRgeb91BQvpGg)

Tap the release button gently as you push back the latch to explore when you have a good contact where the button does not slip off the edge of the latch.

Try to take some well lit  video of the procedure.  If it works, someone else may need itin the future.

Another option to make a thin shim would be to cut up an aluminum soft drink can.  The aluminum is so thin that you can cut it with a pair of kitchen sissors. However, the thinnest shim is going to be the razor blade

CC @revel_flo, @Landwheel_Jason
```

## \#518 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-07T04:47:23.885Z Reads: 24

```
@BearBoi:

Lets assume the latch is tilted in a way that it is weged in place.

That means we will need to cut the latch.

Can you ask Jason to ship you a new latch and an extra cover plate for the ESC enclosuer.  We want the cover plate just in case it is already damaged.  

The latch is a small part that should be easy to cut and replace.  but don't cut it now or you will have nothing to drive.

When you have the spare parts, I'm going to have you insert an exacto knife blade like this

![image|211x219](upload://xLEJWTwszlWPmrTaIw1U2KNFXmB.png) 

 The blades need to be mounted in the proper knife handle.  Then insert the blade to the left of the latch and use a small hammer to tap the blade to the right. Hammer as close as possible to the latch.  If yo ulike, you can put some duct tape or masking tape on the battery to protect it from getting scratched.

We will use some cooking oil as a cutting lubricant. Just a little bit of oil to coat the blade so it cuts and slides better.  Polycarbonate is oil resistant and we are going to clean all the oil off right away anyway.  

Once you slice through the latch, leave the knife blade in between the two cut halves so that the broken part of the latch does not spring up into the battery cavity.  The battery should then slide out.

Wear some leather gloves to protect your hands and never slice towards you.  Always stand on the dull side of the blade and hammer away from you.

I think a dozen light taps should slice through the latch

Do you feel comfortable wiht that procedure.  If so, please contact Jason for the two parts.

CC:

@revel_flo
@Landwheel_Jason
```

## \#520 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-07T05:36:31.863Z Reads: 24

```
@dareno

Here are two battery hacks:

 https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/t/landwheel-l3-x-reviews/45697/430

 https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/t/landwheel-l3-x-reviews/45697/460

A landwheel L3-x will run of of just about any 36 volt battery, however, you uneed to bypass the BMS becasue if it wired through the BMS then the ESC will get fried the first time the BMS disconnects the power. 

also, Andrew Penman lives in Australia and has a few Landwheels.  You could connect with him on facebook or youtube to see if he has any functioning LW batteries.

https://www.facebook.com/search/top/?q=Andrew%20Penman

https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XB79c1khdTE

Either that or sell your Landwheel for parts and order a Revel Kit.  There is good demand for L3-x ESC and drive assemblies.
```

## \#523 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-07T15:38:43.400Z Reads: 25

```
@BearBoi:
Send a PM to @Landwheel_Jason  with your shipping details and email address.

CC me and @revel_flo on the PM.  I'll copy and paste the info to Jason on Skype and in an email with a CC to you (just incase he does not get the PM notification).

I have already sent him a list of parts.

1) Latch
2) Polycarbonate ESC cover  (the part you remove to access the ESC)
3)Battery button
4) Rectangular battery button spring.
5) Rubber USB cover (Bear Bois says it has fallen off)

The ESC cover is removed easily with just six screws.  No glue.

When it comes time to cut the latch  I think this is the safest way to secure the kit and stay clear of the blade:
1)  put the skateboard upside down on a carpet or on soft ground
2)  Put your feet on each tip of the skateboard to hold the work in place
3)  Hold the knife handle in your left hand with a thick leather glove.
4) Insert the lubricated blade into the latch cutting position
5) Drape a cloth over the battery to protect it  or tape folded cardboard into place.  Or put the knife through a rectangle of cardboard before you  insert the blade  to the left of the latch.
6)  Hammer lightly with your lright hand. Staying close to the latch
7) Make sure there is nothing behind the blade to get sliced if the blade breaks.  Keep you feet and ankles far from the blade.  Lean your butt up against a wall or sit in a chair if you need more blance.

Please show these precautions in  your video.
Compare the broken latch to the new latch.  I think the eyelets will be broken.
```

## \#529 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-09T06:51:17.456Z Reads: 23

```
So when you get back on the road again be much more careful with cold weather.  Voltage can drop very quickly with small batteries in cold weather.  Normally, the first vibration means stop immediately.  In cold weather, I don't think you should ride past 50%.  That means you would stop long before the first vibration alert.  I have similar comments on hard uphill accelertion in cold weather.  Hard accelleration causes battery voltage to drop quicky.  The drop in voltage would be more rapid in very cold weather.  So hard uphill acceleration in very cold weather with less than 50% battery would be a triple bad combination.
```

---
## \#530 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-09T06:57:30.741Z Reads: 21

```
I remember wiht my L3-x.  I tried riding it in 0 degree weather.  I could only make it around the block before the battery started fading and vibrating.  So I stopped riding in cold weather.  I'm not trying to blame you for these problems.  But we all have to pay attention to what works and does not work.  The batteries are the most vulnerable part of any electric skateboard.
```

## \#532 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-09T07:03:52.772Z Reads: 21

```
Like I said, I'm not trying to blame you.  These boards and batteries are designed tested in China, not sweeden.   One of my cars is a Nissan Leaf.  It has a massive battery and it also has a battery heater for cold weather.  Electric skateboards do not have battery heaters.  We might not think of these things ahead of time but when a battery fails in colder weather, we need to re-evaluate the reasonable limits of a small lithium battery.

I'm going to give some thought to whats happened and perhaps write up a warning for other customers.
```

---
## \#533 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-09T07:21:47.162Z Reads: 23

```
One more thing to think about.  Low speed mode might not offer much protection.  Lithium batteries recover voltage after you let off the throttle.  So riding on low speed mode might allow you to deplete the battery much more before you hit a vibration alert.  I think its hard to explain but if low battery threashold is 36, then low speed mode could let you deplete to 37 without a vibration, then the battery recovers to 38, then you deplete to 37 with some light throttle,  The ESC is going to reduce acceleration to maintain voltage.  If you travel a good distance this way then the charge could be much more depleted than is indicated by the voltage.  The recovered voltage is a very shallow charge.  

Think of a car battery.  If you crank in cold weather, the battery may drop from 14 volts down to 10.  when you stop cranking, the battery may recover to 13 volts but its a very shallow 13 volt charge. If you measure the battery wiht a volt meter then it looks like a fully charged battery.  But if you measure the battery under load with a cold cranking amps meter, then you see just how shallow the charge is.

An ESC measures only voltage to identify the charge level of the battery.  So the recovered voltage can be misleading to the ESC.  Cold weather and low speed mode might be a bad combination because it could delay the vibration alert.
```

---

## \#535 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-09T17:01:10.469Z Reads: 20

```
Once a battery is damaged it is doomed.  I after overdepleting one LW battery, I was aboe to resurect it by boosting from another LW battery.  However it only lasted another week and it was dangerous because it caused spontaneous braking.  The only thing you could do wiht the kit battery is to disassemble it, charge each cell wiht a single cell charger, then test each cell and replace the damaged cells.  I've never tried it with a revel kit battery.  I judt know that in theory its possible.  Personally, I would rather see the drive and battery returned to Jason so that he can reverse engineere how the battery got stuck.
```

## \#539 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-11T01:19:21.365Z Reads: 26

```
@BearBoi
Now that I have the production revel Kit, I;ve studied it in great detail and I'm starting to think that there is nothing wrong with you battery.  I'm wondering if when you put your hand on the back of the battery, you are actually holding the battery and the drive at the same time.  The battery only stick up about 1/4 inch from the back of the drive.  I wonder if you re putting your hand on the back of the drive and pulling forward  thinking that you are pulling on the battery. 

So instead of putting you hand on the back of the unit, place your palm on the very top of the battery and slide forward as you push down the release button.

If that does not work, do what Flo said and get a friend to help you.  

I really really can't see how the latch could have been broken on the production model.  The prototype was very fragile so I totally understand how the latch can jam on it.  But the production model should be bullet proof.
```

## \#540 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-11T01:36:35.494Z Reads: 25

```
[quote="FredXanadu, post:537, topic:45697"]
i suspect a problem with my battery, i can‚Äôt reach more than 40km/h with 90mm wheels
[/quote]

Unfortunately, I've never tried the standard size battery.  I would say it's 80/20 that the standard battery is capable of less speed or that your battery is not as strong as it should be.

The 
context that I have is that the L3-x was never strong enough to carry me more than 2 - 4 kilometers until I started doubling the  batteries.  Also the V2 was completely useless with its original battery but it turned out to be a really impressive skateboard if you did the work to substitute a V4 battery.

Small batteries can make excellent skateboards function very poorly.  Larger batteries can turn useless skateboards into  long range rockets.

Here is some more info.  as a 200 lb rider, I could get 17 kilometers of range out of either the 4wd L3-x or the 2WD kit prototype.  But if I rode flat-out, with hard acceleration and at top speed then I could get as little as 6 km of range on either machine.  So I could totally see how a smaller battery could give you not much more than 4 km of range if you are are riding fast and accelerating hard.

I should also point out that if a battery is damaged, you really can't go anywhere on it.  It should  only take you one or two blocks or maybey less.

So I think in the end, you need to buy the extended range battery.  If you are disappointed with the standard range battery, I think Jason would give you a special price on the extended range batteries.  If I were you, I'd order two and ask for a discount based on the standard range battery not meeting your needs or expectations.

I suspect that if you have Jason ship you another standard range battery that you will just be disappointed again. I suspect your weight and riding style are not consistent with what the standard range battery has to offer.

Again, I have ot say that i'm guessing because I have never ridden a standard range battery.
```

---
## \#541 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-11T02:59:08.303Z Reads: 23

```
[quote="FredXanadu, post:537, topic:45697"]
i can‚Äôt reach more than 40km/h with 90mm wheels
[/quote]

Hey Fred:

Befor you give up on standard range batteries, try one little experiment.  I have a theory that setting the wheel size on the remote may actually affect the top speed.  So for example 110 mm wheels as a setting may limit the max RPM to less than it would be with a 90mm setting.  

So set the remote wheel size setting  to the minimum size and see if it improves your actual top speed.

Look at GPS/Phone speed, not the remote speed indicator.
```

```
i don't think the problem come from from the button, the battery seems to large now, i can only move them to 1mm...

Edit : after one hour and the help from a friend the battery is unstuck.
Check the video for the unstuck tip
https://youtu.be/9IEKumGTBO4
```

## \#552 Posted by: FredXanadu Posted at: 2019-10-13T16:10:11.941Z Reads: 21

```
1) if you look attentively the video, my friend first only push the button, the battery don't slide... It starts to slide when he clamps the button between his fingers. it"s a key point of the procedure.
2) your girlfriend NEED TO CLAMP BETWEEN HER FINGERS the button
3) you pull the battery with your 2 hands, your feet under the truck to have a good leverage.

You don't need to brute force only to be synchronized.

PS : I rode 120 kms of the parisian streets :slight_smile: 

Try again, you'll win this time !
```

## \#553 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-15T04:56:41.662Z Reads: 23

```
[quote="BearBoi, post:549, topic:45697"]
As for lubrication, would armor-all be my best bet?
[/quote]

@BearBoi:
Armor All is a silicone based spray that is designed for plastic and makes plastic very slipery.  Thats why I suggested it. In general Polycarbonate is very oil and chemical resistant.  

In addition to fred's video technique, what about using a little leverage.  This is a 2x3  but  a 2x4 or 2x2 would also work.  Just put the tip of the board into the notch on the back of the battery and lever against the motors while simultaneoulsy pushing on the battery button.  I don't think you should need to push hard on the battery button.

![image|641x480](upload://bB4a5p3bsqjoiUfDfbG3kVqp4CC.jpeg)
```

## \#555 Posted by: BearBoi Posted at: 2019-10-17T08:31:54.062Z Reads: 23

```
Getting help to attempt it today. Will update tonight. My battery seems to work fine though. Not sure how to know if any damage has been done.

I have learned to live with revel batteries in my climate. Like you said, never ride far or push it hard in cold. Another thing that helps a lot, and I have had 0 issues since doing this. Keep the battery warm and plug it into a charger as soon as I get home. Also keep the board in a warm spot and keep it warm with body heat, heaters, towels. Whatever is nearby.

I also am very careful about not idling for long or cruising for long in situations I know it will get cold. I don't think there is any damage to the battery, I have had no issues for a week now since I really payed attention to maintaining my kit.
```

---
## \#556 Posted by: pkasanda Posted at: 2019-10-17T08:38:30.376Z Reads: 24

```
If your voltage fresh off the charger is  the same for both batteries then both should be fine.  The correct voltage for the L3-x batteries was 41 - 41.5.

I remember wrapping scarves and clear food wrap around my L3-x batteriy & drive so that I coud do some late season testing.  But I only did that once because my L3-x arrived  in December.  That was back in 2017.

Best not to push your luck with cold weather.
```

## \#558 Posted by: BearBoi Posted at: 2019-10-20T11:49:27.931Z Reads: 22

```
@FredXanadu and @pkasanda I got the battery unstuck this weekend. It is very tight, but I found a technique that works for me.

I used a long metal shoehorn for leverage and pushed on the back of the battery instead of pulling. Cleaned it and put it back, stuck right away. Seems I always need to use the shoehorn.  Works for now though :) I'll look into lubricating and or lightly sanding it in the future. For now this works.

My kit is more alive than ever and I will write a proper review of my whole experience soon.
```

## \#559 Posted by: Byronel Posted at: 2019-11-06T09:32:14.608Z Reads: 22

```
Hi guys. I just wanted to post an update with regards to the team at landwheel.

I have a really bad unit that eventually ended with a broken axle. This was at the time Landwheel stopped and started development of the new Revel kit. At the time Jason said to me he would replace my device with the new one once its developed.

Its been a year later and true to his word, Jason replaced it :slight_smile:
There are not many people in this world that stick to there word so this was a brethe of fresh air.

I want to publicly thank Jason and the Landwheel/ Revel team.

As for the device..... Its really good :) 
I have only had a few trips on the board but from what I can gather, its much better!
The new batteries are trustworthy the option of using all 4 skate wheels (Like boosted) is really smooth. 

From my experience, I hope Revel take off. The customer service is something I can vouch for :)
```
